## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring forces), velocity v (damping), and time t (possible driving). The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and/or external periodic driving.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity, asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type damping)
- Parametrically driven oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (Mathieu equation)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving force)
- Combined nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * (1 - x**2) * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Van der Pol-Duffing)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (sign-dependent friction approximation)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear restoring from pendulum dynamics)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v (asymmetric oscillator with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x²) → asymmetric potential wells indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v → self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Periodic functions of time (sin/cos(c*t)) → external driving forces causing resonance or chaos
- Product of position powers and velocity (x²*v) → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type systems
- Cubic position terms with sign opposite to linear term → Duffing-type hardening or softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system (conservative or dissipative but undriven)
- Sinusoidal function of position sin(c*x) → pendulum-like dynamics with multiple equilibria
- Odd functions of velocity in damping → energy dissipation consistent with time-reversal symmetry breaking
- Product of time-periodic term with position → parametric excitation (Mathieu/Floquet instabilities)
